AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: I can hear
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 10/23/2002 05:45:34 PM
-----
BODY:
It's amazing. My clothes rustle disconcertingly when I walk. I can hear the pads of my fingers scraping on the piano keys. By contrast my left ear - the one that the nurse didn't remove a huge brown plug of wax from - now feels blocked, so I'm going to drip oil in it for the next few days and see the nurse again next week.

EMAIL: ahmed@baizid.org
IP: 62.212.97.139
URL: 
DATE: 11/16/2002 11:13:49 PM
Step 9, 10 and 11.
There is no test file in CVS but there is an addressbook sample.

9. xindice ac -c /db -n addressbook
10. xindice ad -c /db/addressbook -f java/examples/guide/xml/address1.xml
11. xindice xpath -c /db/addressbook -q "//person[@fname='John']"

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Tom
EMAIL: tom@throwingbeans.org
IP: 217.158.178.98
URL: http://www.throwingbeans.org
DATE: 01/02/2003 12:29:20 PM
Hi Francesco

"could not find out home directory"

This means that you need to set the environment variables that CVS uses to locate your home directory.

Here's a link with more information:

http://ccvs.cvshome.org/fom/cache/194.html

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Never Eat a Tomato
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 11/08/2002 12:03:02 AM
-----
BODY:
Søren drove up from London and we spent the evening working on a soundtrack for a proposed animation of <a href = "http://www.amazon.co.uk/exec/obidos/ASIN/184121602X/">one of Lauren's books</a>.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<img alt="soren.jpg" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/soren.jpg" width="240" height="180" border="0" align = "right" />The result (click <a href = "/music/tomato_cut.mp3">here</a> for a 20 second snippet) is rather melancholy for children's TV, but I like it. 

I'm also very pleased with my new, minaturised studio, which sound technology obsessives will have already identified as the OS X version of <a href = "http://www.emagic.de">Logic Platinum</a> on a <a href = "http://apple.com/powerbook">G4 PowerBook</a> and the <a href = "http://www.motu.com">MOTU 828</a> firewire audio interface. All the sounds on this track come from the EXS 24 virtual sampler, apart from Søren's guitar and Maisie's voice. If you play a fine trumpet and live in Oxfordshire, you could come and record the horn section for us.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: On the tab
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 02/19/2003 11:54:27 AM
-----
BODY:
After all the weblog noise on <a href="http://www.petitiononline.com/mod_perl/signed.cgi?safaritb&amp;1">tabbed browsing</a> I'm surprised there hasn't been more fuss made of <a href="http://iterm.sourceforge.net/">iTerm</a>, an open source alternative to the OS X Terminal app. iTerm's tabbed interface means I can flit between SSH sessions on our local and remote Linux boxes without wasting brain cycles locating the relevant terminal window... this honestly makes a significant difference to my working day.

The application I really want to see tabbed is <a href="http://www.barebones.com">BBEdit</a>. I love this editor but having more than two documents open at once makes for a <a href="/images/messyscreen.png">very messy screen</a>.

Update: BBEdit 8, released in September 2004, includes a '<a href = "http://www.barebones.com/products/bbedit/benefitsomnipotence.shtml#DocumentsDrawer">document drawer</a>' feature which approximates a tabbed interface.

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Giles
EMAIL: spam001@gilestv.com
IP: 213.217.165.94
URL: 
DATE: 02/22/2003 08:07:07 PM
Do you know a way to get Cold Fusion Studio (or something similar) to do that cool FTP save thing via SSH?
-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: tom
EMAIL: tom@throwingbeans.org
IP: 213.78.122.41
URL: http://www.throwingbeans.org
DATE: 02/24/2003 07:51:07 AM
Giles - you'll need to create an SSH tunnel between your machine and the FTP server, and then point your FTP client (ColdFusion Studio) to localhost. The syntax for creating the tunnel is:

ssh -L 21:yourftpserver.com:21 -l accountname yourftpserver.com

Note that 'accountname' above is *not* your FTP username, but rather what you'd use to log into the FTP server via SSH. 

You could use <a href="http://www.chiark.greenend.org.uk/~sgtatham/putty/download.html" rel="nofollow">Putty</a> to set up the SSH tunnel for you. Either way, once it's up you'll need to point your FTP client to 'localhost' (i.e. your side of the tunnel) and use your normal FTP details. 
-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Giles
EMAIL: spam001@gilestv.com
IP: 139.191.42.22

-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Tom
EMAIL: tom@throwingbeans.org
IP: 217.158.178.103
URL: http://throwingbeans.org
DATE: 02/25/2003 05:41:37 PM
Ah, well if your remote server isn't running FTP then it won't work. SSH tunnelling simply secures an otherwise insecure transport (it's typically used to bypass a firewall which restricts port 21 but not port 22, for example). Perhaps you could ask your sysadmin to install an FTP daemon on the server, but restrict the port with a firewall or <a href="http://www.ankitfadia.com/tcpwrap.htm" rel="nofollow">TCP Wrappers</a>.

STATUS: Publish

CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 02/20/2003 11:00:42 AM

BODY:
Dave Maddison from <a href="http://www.bea.com">BEA</a> sent me <a href="http://dev2dev.bea.com/articlesnews/discussion/thread.jsp?thread=DJ_003">this link</a> about XMLBeans, their new technology which facilitates typed access to XML documents from Java. BEA provide a nice web service which returns XMLBeans classes from user-submitted schemas; apart from this I can't spot any advantages over existing data binding tools like <a href="http://castor.exolab.org/xml-framework.html">Castor</a> and <a href="http://zeus.enhydra.org/">Zeus</a> (I'm sure Dave will tell me some). Even better, he'll start a blog of his own so I can keep up to date on these things.

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Dave
EMAIL: me@davidmaddison.com
IP: 81.6.242.11
URL: http://www.davidmaddison.com
DATE: 02/24/2003 12:30:28 AM
The XMLBeans has an FAQ question regarding the difference between such things as Castor, here : http://dev2dev.bea.com/techtrack/xmlbeans/xmlbeans.jsp?highlight=xmlbeansfaq#2.b

In short there are three main differences between XMLBeans and other technologies (according to the FAQ :-).<ol>  <li>XMLBeans cover the XMLSchema 100%. <li>The XML isn't thrown away, it's fully accessible underneath the beans. <li>Marshalling and Un marshalling happens on demand, so there is an increase in performance.</li></li></li></ol>

So what exactly IS a chowder?
-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: ian
EMAIL: ian@monami.org
IP: 217.158.178.97
URL: http://www.monami.org
DATE: 02/26/2003 03:44:30 PM
Derived from the French <em>chaudi&egravere</em> - a fisherman's cooking pot - a chowder is a good 'n chunky seafood soup, the most famous being clam chowder.

You can enjoy a chowder New England stylee with cream or New York stylee with tomatoes, if that's what floats your boat.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Transformation Inspiration
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: textile_1
ALLOW PINGS: 1
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 03/03/2003 12:37:33 AM
-----
BODY:
16 dreary hours writing an XSL stylesheet to convert a 2000-node XML document into HTML yielded two discoveries and an idea:

* <a href = "http://xmlsoft.org/XSLT.html">LibXSLT</a> is literally twenty times faster than <a href = "http://xml.apache.org/xalan-j/index.html">Xalan-Java</a> for command line transformations of large XML documents (on my OS X 10.2.4 PowerBook, at any rate). 

* Apache's Translet / XSLTC tools have been bundled into Xalan-Java, which making my <a href = "http://torchbox.com/xml/transletwrapper.cfm">TransletWrapper documentation</a> out of date. I plan to write a 'Getting Started with Translets' guide to this underrated technology.

* If you have a good head for recursion you can speed up boring XSLT jobs by writing a stylesheet stylesheet; a transformer transformer. XML publishers could make automatic stylesheet generation easy for XSLT developers by following a node labelling convention... more on this later.
-----

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: PostgreSQL and XML
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 03/12/2003 10:35:01 PM
-----
BODY:
I'm been feeling mildly guilty about not publishing the work I did with <a href = "#" title = "Where are you, John?">John Gray</a> last year on XPath support in <a href = "http://www.postgresql.org" title = "Powerful, robust, extensible RDBMS">PostgreSQL</a>, but the interest in Jon Udell's <a href = "http://weblog.infoworld.com/udell/2003/03/12.html#a637" title = "demonstration of XPath in a SELECT statement against a Virtuoso database">'SQL and XPath'</a> post has goaded me into action: here's a brief outline of the four <a href = "http://www.msif.org" title = "This large, multilingual site stores most of its data as marked-up text in PostgreSQL columns">production-ready</a> XPath functions which represent the most complete XML support of any open source RDBMS.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<p>The four functions extend John's previous work (see contrib/xml directory in any recent Postgres installation) and rely on:

<ul>
<li>Postgres's support of user-defined functions written in C, Perl and PL/SQL.</li>  
<li>The fast, light, C-based libxml library from <a href = "http://xmlsoft.org">xmlsoft.org</a>.</li>  
</ul>

As the example below demonstrates, Postgres UDFs can be used in both the SELECT and WHERE clauses of a SQL statement.</p>

<pre>
CREATE TABLE t_articles (
    article_id int4 NOT NULL,
    article_title varchar(255) NOT NULL,  
    article_xml text
    );
        
INSERT INTO t_articles (article_id, article_title, article_xml)
    VALUES (1, 'Some Beatles', 
    '&lt;beatles id = "b1"&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "guitar" alive = "no"&gt;john lennon&lt;/beatle&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "guitar" alive = "no"&gt;george harrison&lt;/beatle&gt;
    &lt;/beatles&gt;');

INSERT INTO t_articles (article_id, article_title, article_xml)
    VALUES (2, 'Other Beatles', 
    '&lt;beatles id = "b2"&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "bass" alive = "yes"&gt;paul mccartney&lt;/beatle&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "drums" alive = "yes"&gt;ringo starr&lt;/beatle&gt;
    &lt;/beatles&gt;');
 
SELECT 
     article_id, xpath_string(article_xml,'/beatles/@id') AS beatle_id
FROM 
     t_articles 
WHERE 
     xpath_bool(article_xml,'/beatles/beatle[@alive="yes"]');
 
 /*
 --  returns:
 -- 
 --  article_id  |  beatle_id
 -- ------------   -----------
 --  2           |  b2
 */
 </pre>
 
 <p>Usage of the two functions shown here - <i>xpath_string</i> and <i>xpath_bool</i> - should be self-explanatory. They each take two arguments: a column identifier and an XPath statement. <i>xpath_string</i> returns a string (the textual content of a node) and <i>xpath_bool</i> returns a boolean value. <i>xpath_number</i> returns a number, which is useful for numerical comparisons or running mathematical functions on the returned value:</p>

<pre>
WHERE xpath_number(article_xml,'//job_title/@year') > 2001 
</pre>

<p>The fourth function, <i>xpath_nodeset</i>, is a somewhat kludgey solution to the problem of returning values from repeated nodes in a single record. Here's an example of how it might be used: </p>

<pre>
SELECT 
    xpath_nodeset(article_xml,'//beatle/@instrument') AS beatle_instrument
FROM 
    t_articles
WHERE 
    article_id = 2;

 /*
 --  returns:
 -- 
 --  beatle_instrument  
 --  -------------------
 --  &lt;instrument&gt;bass&lt;/instrument&gt;&lt;instrument&gt;drums&lt;/instrument&gt;
 */
</pre>

<p>This problem highlights the potentially awkward marriage between SQL sets and arbitrarily structured data, but I'm sure that better solutions are possible (how does <a href = "http://www.openlinksw.com/" title = "Expensive RDBMS/XML container">Virtuoso</a> handle repeated nodes?). PostgreSQL 7.3 allows UDFs to return multiple rows, which might help... suggestions are very welcome.</p>

<p><a href = "mailto:tomdyson[at]spamcop.net" title = "mangled for spambots">Contact me</a> for the software in its current unlicensed, undocumented state, or watch this space for a properly packaged distribution.</p>

<p>Update: the functions <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/postgresql_and_xml_updated.html">have been updated</a> and are now part of the standard PostgreSQL distribution.</p>
-----
EXCERPT:

If you need such functionality, consider the use of OpenLink Universal Virtuoso Server. It supports XPath, XQuery, XSLT, SQL-XML and many more.

E.g. in the listed example, Virtuoso allows you to use a single xpath_contains() predicate in WHERE clause to filter out documents and retrieve the required part of data from the document as a simgle operation. If needed, special XML-optimized free-text index may be used to perform similar searches in large sets of XML documents without reading all of them during the search. In addition, XML documents may be parsed once and saved in the database in special LOBs so the application don't have to parse or even read from disk a huge document to retrieve a small part.

P.S. HTTP server and client, SOAP, DTD and XmlSchema validators are built in, too.

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Kingsley Idehen
EMAIL: kidehen@openlinks.com
IP: 24.147.186.209
URL: http://www.openlinksw.com/virtuoso/whatis.htm
DATE: 04/21/2003 02:27:19 PM
In response to your question re. Virtuoso, here is how we handle repeating nodes sets.

We handle repeated nodes by returing them as a vector of values :


CREATE TABLE t_articles (     article_id int NOT NULL,     article_title varchar(255) NOT NULL,       article_xml long varchar     );


insert into t_articles (article_id, article_title) values (1, 'a');
insert into t_articles (article_id, article_title) values (2, 'b');

UPDATE t_articles SET article_xml = '
    &lt;beatles id = "b1"&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "guitar" alive = "no"&gt;john lennon&lt;/beatle&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "guitar" alive = "no"&gt;george harrison&lt;/beatle&gt;
    &lt;/beatles&gt;'
WHERE article_id = 1;

UPDATE t_articles SET article_xml = '
    &lt;beatles id = "b2"&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "bass" alive = "yes"&gt;paul mccartney&lt;/beatle&gt;
        &lt;beatle instrument = "drums" alive = "yes"&gt;ringo starr&lt;/beatle&gt;
    &lt;/beatles&gt;'
WHERE article_id = 2;

SELECT  xpath_eval('//beatle/@instrument', xml_tree_doc (article_xml), 0) AS beatle_instrument FROM      t_articles WHERE      article_id = 2;


The repeating nodes are returned as part of a vector (the third arg to xpath_eval = 0 (which means get all nodes)).

Otherwise: 

SELECT  xpath_eval('//beatle/@instrument', xml_tree_doc (article_xml), 1) AS beatle_instrument FROM      t_articles WHERE      article_id = 2;

I'll get the first node set ('bass').

So to conclude we either get a particular node set (third_xpath_eval_arg > 0) or we get them all as a vector (third_xpath_eval_arg = 0)

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: My Enemy
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 03/30/2003 08:20:20 PM
-----
BODY:
The Guardian joins the <a href = "http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/technology/2881491.stm">BBC</a> in highlighting <a href = "http://www.dear_raed.blogspot.com">The Baghdad Blogger</a>, whose last entry was posted on March 24th; hopefully this recent silence is only a result of the coalition's destruction of Baghdad's communications centre. The resonance of this man's personal, provoking account of life in a bombed city reminds me of an unfinished - in fact hardly started - project called 'My Enemy'. This was to be a moderated internet forum enabling and motivating the citizens of countries at war to communicate with each other across military lines, leveraging the relative anonymity of web applications to bypass war propaganda that seeks to dehumanise the enemy. Despite a decent domain name and some interest from the <a href = "http://www.icrc.org">International Red Cross</a> nothing ever happened to this project; objections over the feasibility of policing a non-political debate weighed heavily against it. But armed with the evidence that the daily details of a blogger's life can affect the mindsets of a hundred thousand Westerners, I'm going to try again. 
-----
EXTENDED BODY:

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Unwritten
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: textile_1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 05/30/2003 01:09:26 AM
-----
BODY:
Summaries of never-written entries for April and May:

* *Weapons of Mouse Destruction*
The failure of our humane mouse traps and the dramatic success of the nasty type; ruminations on my swift innurement to handling dead mice.

* *Spongers*
The joy of bodyboarding in New South Wales and <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/surfer_tom.html" title = "Sofia took this on her P800 mobile phone" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/surfer_tom.html','popup','width=320,height=240,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">Perranporth</a>, Cornwall. Advances in wetsuit technology. 

* *Adventurers*
My sister returns to a remote village in north east India for field work on her PhD thesis, Søren goes to Baghdad for Channel 4, Tom Le Quesne <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/afghanifishers.html" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/afghanifishers.html','popup','width=300,height=343,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">fishes for trout</a> in Afghanistan.

* <b>PostgreSQL and XSLT</b>
Our <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/tech/postgresql_and_xml.html">XPath extensions for Postgres</a> now include better support for returning multiple rows and fast XSLT transformations within the database. 

* *Gravalax*
<a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/deadtrout_small.html" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/deadtrout_small.html','popup','width=500,height=375,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">Hunter-gathering in Devon</a>

* *30 years*
My birthday was also Sofia's due date, but the baby didn't show... We had a lovely day in the garden with friends. <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/birthday.html" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/birthday.html', 'popup', 'width=240,height=180,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">690Kb film, Flash MX required</a>

* *Scilly Weekend*
Three days on <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/scilly_sof.html" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/scilly_sof.html','popup','width=500,height=375,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">St Agnes</a> for the gig-racing championships.

* *Latent Semantic Indexing*
Magic technology, ideas for usage in social software.

* *Shakey*
Ben, Mihai, Søren and I saw Neil Young playing his dodgy new concept album and beautiful old favourites at the Hammersmith Apollo:  

* *Python*
A lovely language, concise and complete; I've rewritten <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/tech/ewab.html">EWAB</a> in it.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Search::ContextGraph
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: textile_1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 07/18/2003 08:20:39 AM
-----
BODY:
Many thanks to <a href = "http://www.idlewords.com">Maciej Ceglowski</a> ("<a href = "http://laughingmeme.org/archives/000547.html">lead troublemaker in the LSI revolution</a>"); his swift response to my change requests for Search::ContextGraph means that I now have a working framework for retrieving - and persisting - document relatedness.

More on this very soon. In the meantime next-generation search wannabees should check out:

* The paper on <a href = "http://www.nitle.org/papers/Contextual_Network_Graphs.pdf">Spreading Activation Search</a> by Maciej and his colleagues.

* <a href = "http://search.cpan.org/author/MCEGLOWS/Search-ContextGraph-0.05/">Search::ContextGraph</a> on CPAN

* _Foundations of Statistical Natural Language Processing_, by Manning and Schultz (<a href = "http://www.amazon.co.uk/exec/obidos/ASIN/0262133601/">Amazon UK link</a>)

* <a href = "http://javelina.cet.middlebury.edu/lsa/out/lsa_intro.htm">Introduction to Latent Semantic Indexing</a>

* Tim Bray's <a href = "http://www.tbray.org/ongoing/When/200x/2003/06/15/OnSearch">masterclass series</a> on search engine development

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: MailBucket
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 09/30/2003 09:58:21 AM
-----
BODY:
I'm pleased to announce MailBucket, a public service email-to-RSS gateway. In a nutshell, the last 10 emails sent to <i>foo</i>@mailbucket.org will be available as RSS at http://mailbucket.org/<i>foo</i>.xml, where you choose <i>foo</i>. A background and further instructions are available at <a href = "http://www.mailbucket.org/">mailbucket.org</a>; please use the comments feature below for bug reports, feature requests and expressions of enthusiasm.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:

-----
EXCERPT:

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Viswanath Gondi
EMAIL: gondi@mailcity.com
IP: 172.169.20.216
URL: http://blogs.law.harvard.edu/vgondi
DATE: 09/30/2003 08:42:00 PM
Great app, I've been waiting for it for a long time. The service could be even more useful if the rss feeds were split by the sender address. For example, if I send an emails from  foo@mailinglist.com to email2rss@mailbucket.org, the emails get aggregated in http://mailbucket.org/fooATmailinglist.com.xml

Advantages: 
Spam gets automatically filtered.
People using your site can find more feeds that interest them. 
Reduce duplication of feeds on the server.
You can setup a pay per address model for the current configuration.
Lots of data locked in inaccessible mailing lists will be fed into google.

But be sure to post a notice saying that you can only subscribe the feeds that can be publicly distributed.
Once again, great work!!!!!

A new test results is shown in "slurp" (linked
to this message): The parser doesn't translate
character [amp] "&amp;" to [amp]amp; "&amp;amp;" -
this can have strange side effects.

IMO translating all [amp] "&amp;" before doing 
anything else like looking for links should work.
And _after_ processing the links all remaining 
[lt] "&lt;" could be translated to [amp]lt; "&amp;lt;"

At the moment it's possible to insert XML contructs
into the XML resp. simple HTML output with these 
characters.

COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Mike Brown
EMAIL: mike@hyperreal.org
IP: 65.101.207.237
URL: 
DATE: 05/30/2004 02:04:55 AM
LiveJournal has an option that lets users create pseudo-accounts that are fed by RSS or Atom feeds. I used this feature today to set up 
http://www.livejournal.com/users/farber_ip/, which is fed by http://www.mailbucket.org/interesting-people.xml. LJ users "friend" these syndicated accounts and monitor them as they would any other friend's journal.

I am noticing that the feed you create is apparently just passing the raw emails through. Unfortunately, the messages are sometimes sent with Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable, which, if not decoded, results in a feed that is, uh, quoted-unreadable. Given that decoding quoted-printable is not something even an aggregator would do, I would like to request that you do the decoding on your end.

For example, see http://www.mailbucket.org/interesting-people-296391.html. The original message had the quoted-printable header, so ideally you should pipe the text through a decoder such as the one built in to python's quopri module.

Also, I note that the feed adds a "mark this message as spam" link to the message, as can be seen in http://www.livejournal.com/users/farber_ip/1499.html. Given that dumb/malicious users and robots/crawlers/spiders will likely activate these links for every message, you might want to consider removing the link or somehow filtering out such hits.

Thanks,
Mike
-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Mike Brown
EMAIL: mike@hyperreal.org
IP: 65.101.207.237
URL: 
DATE: 05/30/2004 02:30:01 AM
Another thing to note: The messages sent to the interesting-people list all contain a footer with a link that the recipient can use to unsubscribe or manage their list subscription options. Since the link gets republished in the interesting-people feed generated by MailBucket, if you have not yet set a password on that site, you might want to do that ASAP. Someone, or some robot, will certainly attempt to click through, sooner or later.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: .NET on Panther
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 01/14/2004 06:11:07 PM
-----
BODY:
Six steps to installing a C# compiler on OS X 10.3, using Rotor.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
1. Download the SSCLI from Microsoft

<pre>wget http://download.microsoft.com/download/.netframesdk/CLI3/1.0/WXP/EN-US/sscli_20021101.tgz
tar xfz sscli_20021101.tgz
cd sscli</pre>

2. Download the patches for Panther in the same directory

<pre>wget http://www.mondrian-script.org/rotor/panther_mark2_diffs.txt.gz
gunzip panther_mark2_diffs.txt.gz
</pre>

3. Apply the patches

<pre>patch -p1 < panther_mark2_diffs.txt</pre>

4. Set environment variables

<pre>source env.csh (CSH or TCSH) source env.sh (BASH)</pre>

4. Compile (took just over an hour for me)

<pre>./buildall</pre>

5. Set environment variables again (I'm not sure why I had to do this)

<pre>source env.csh (CSH or TCSH) source env.sh (BASH)</pre>

6. Try the samples

<pre>cd samples/hello
csc hello.cs
clix hello.exe</pre>

7. Read readfirst.html in the root of your installation

I haven't tried installing Mono or Portable .NET on Panther; do let me know if you have.

Mono: <a href = "http://www.go-mono.com/">http://www.go-mono.com/</a>
Portable .NET: <a href = "http://www.gnu.org/projects/dotgnu/pnet.html">http://www.gnu.org/projects/dotgnu/pnet.html</a>
Microsoft SSCLI: <a hrf = "http://msdn.microsoft.com/net/sscli/">http://msdn.microsoft.com/net/sscli/</a>
-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:

-----

TITLE: Self-propulsion
STATUS: Publish

Yesterday Matilda worked out how to move herself along the ground. She uses a side-on dragging technique, pushing out with her left leg and pulling forwards on the carpet with her left hand. Every few paces she re-orientates herself with her right hand and starts again. It's wonderful to see.

Here she is in action: <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/drag_modem.html" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/drag_modem.html', 'popup', 'width=320,height=240,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">low bandwidth</a> / <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/drag_bb.html" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/drag_bb.html', 'popup', 'width=320,height=240,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">medium bandwidth</a>. AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: XML databases with eXist and ColdFusion
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 09/15/2004 03:24:33 PM
-----
BODY:
<a href = "http://exist.sourceforge.net/">eXist</a> is the first open source XML database to support XQuery, a query language whose specification is still in <a href = "http://www.w3.org/TR/xquery/">draft</a>, but apparently approaching finality.

eXist is the first product to meet <a href = "http://www.torchbox.com/">Torchbox</a>'s requirements for an XML repository in environments where our <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/tech/postgresql_and_xml.html">Postgres/XPath</a> combination is not viable; for example when the client specifies a Windows platform or an Oracle or SQL Server back-end:

<ul><li>Open source</li>
<li>Cross-platform</li>
<li>Support for XQuery (XPath doesn't cut it for many basic content management tasks)</li>
<li>Adequate performance</li></ul>

As a bonus, eXist provides a very simple and effective REST API. Here's a ColdFusion component which abstracts that API a little further:

<a href = "/xmldb.cfc">xmldb.cfc</a>
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
And here's an example usage:

&lt;cfset xmldb_uri = "http://localhost:8080/exist/servlet/db/beat_combos/"&gt;
&lt;cfset mydoc = '&lt;beatles&gt;
&lt;beatle id = "1"&gt;john&lt;/beatle&gt;&lt;beatle id = "2"&gt;paul&lt;/beatle&gt;
&lt;/beatles&gt;'&gt;

&lt;cfset xmldb = createobject("component", "xmldb")&gt;

&lt;!--- insert an XML document ---&gt;
&lt;cfset xmldb.insertXML(xmldb_uri, mydoc, "beatles")&gt;

&lt;!--- return results of XQuery statement ---&gt;
&lt;cfset myquery = "//beatle"&gt;
&lt;cfdump var = "#xmldb.execute(xmldb_uri, myquery)#"&gt;

&lt;!--- move document within database ---&gt;
&lt;cfset xmldb.moveXML(xmldb_uri, "beatles", "beatles2")&gt;

&lt;!--- delete moved document from database ---&gt;
&lt;cfset xmldb.deleteXML(xmldb_uri, "beatles2")&gt;

The XML2Query() method which is optionally invoked by xmldb.execute() is a reworking of my old <a href = "http://www.torchbox.com/xml/toolkit.cfm">XML query tag</a> which returns a ColdFusion recordset from an XPath query. Handling data-orientated XML documents like relational tables still seems a very convenient model to me; I'm surprised there aren't analogs in other languages.
-----

-----

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: File-based caching in ColdFusion
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 2
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 11/11/2004 05:13:18 PM
-----
BODY:
I've extended Brandon Purcell's <a href = "http://www.bpurcell.org/blog/index.cfm?mode=entry&ENTRY=963">custom tag for in-memory caching</a> so that cached content can be optionally stored in the file system, rather than in shared memory. 
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
This update to the documentation explains the new functionality:

"File-based caching reduces the performance advantages of in-memory caching, but will still yield significant improvements  in most cases (file IO is almost always cheaper than database access, for example) and exerts minimal impact on your application's memory requirements. CACHEDIR must be a ColdFusion-writeable directory and should be stored outside the web root if your cache contains sensitive content. It is recommended that STRIPWHITESPACE is set to 'true' when file-based caching is enabled, to minimise file IO. Note that the Application scope is still used to persist cache meta-data (scriptname and expiry).

CF_Accelerate will recreate a file-based cache automatically when the appropriate file is unavailable, making it possible to flush the cache by removing files from ATTRIBUTES.CACHEDIR. The usual methods of cache flushing - adding 'flushAccelerator=true' to the URL; through the <a href = "http://www.bpurcell.org/blog/index.cfm?mode=entry&entry=1045">CF_Accelerate Management Interface</a> - are still available."

Version 1.4 of CF_Accelerate, which contains this update, can be downloaded <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/cf_accelerate_1.4.zip">here</a>.
-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:

-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Danny
EMAIL: datspam@2gen.net
IP: 24.215.45.225

DATE: 11/11/2004 08:11:46 PM
Is this the correct usage?

&lt;cf_accelerate cachedWithin="#createTimeSpan(0,0,20,0)#" StripWhitespace="true" CACHEDir="\cacheContent\"&gt;

Where cacheContent is a subdirectory within the current website...
-----
COMMENT:
AUTHOR: Tom Dyson
EMAIL: tom@torchbox.com
IP: 213.78.162.207
URL: http://www.throwingbeans.org
DATE: 11/11/2004 10:11:58 PM
Danny, you need to provide the full path to your cache directory, including the trailing slash. For example:

cacheDir="D:\inetpub\cacheContent\"

or 

cacheDir="/usr/local/apache/cacheContent/"

You may want to specify a directory which is outside the web root, to prevent the contents of your cache files from being accessed directly.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Using XML-RPC libraries to share complex variables
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 05/20/2005 12:48:18 PM
-----
BODY:
<a href = "http://www.openwddx.org/" title = "moribund project site for WDDX">WDDX</a> - an open standard for serialising complex variables into a portable XML format - was a good idea that never took off. We were talking about this at work when I realised that XML-RPC, for which libraries are built in or easily available to most modern languages, requires exactly this functionality. Some implementations might need a little work to strip out or mock up the unwanted transport layer, but in most cases you only need a few lines of code to switch between complex variables and a portable XML string. 
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<br /><br />Here are examples in Python, Perl and Ruby - run them piped together like this:<br /><br />

<strong>./xmlrpc.py | ./xmlrpc.pl | ./xmlrpc.rb</strong><br /><br />

Could XML-RPC offer the marshalling standard that REST is looking for?<br /><br />

Python:
<pre>
import xmlrpclib

orwell={'1': 'All languages are equal'}
print xmlrpclib.dumps(tuple([orwell]),methodresponse=1)
</pre>

Perl (needs <a href = "http://search.cpan.org/~byrne/SOAP-Lite-0.65_5/">SOAP-Lite</a>):
<pre>
use XMLRPC::Lite;

undef $/; $package = <>;
$data = XMLRPC::Deserializer->deserialize($package);
@args = $data->valueof("params");
%orwell=%{$args[0][0]};
$orwell{'2'}='But some languages are more equal than others';
print XMLRPC::Serializer->envelope('response', 'null',\%orwell);
</pre>

Ruby:
<pre>
require "xmlrpc/marshal"

depacket = XMLRPC::Marshal.load(STDIN.gets)
for key in depacket.keys()
        puts depacket[key]
end
</pre>

<p>Update: there's prior art <a href = "http://www.decafbad.com/blog/2002/04/26/oooabg">here</a> and <a href = "http://radio.weblogs.com/0113297/2003/10/01.html#a236">here</a>.</p>
-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:

STATUS: Publish

<img alt="charlie and lola" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/c_an_l.gif" width="160" height="150" style="padding:4px;  border:1px solid #ddd; margin:4px;" align = "right" />The work that Søren and I started on a soundtrack for Charlie and Lola in <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/rec/never_eat_a_tomato.html">November 2002</a> is now playing to a projected audience of 80 million children on the <a href = "http://disney.go.com/disneychannel/playhouse/charlieandlola/index.html">Disney Playhouse</a> channel. It launches in the UK on BBC2 and CBeebies this autumn; it's been sold to TF1 (France), Sweden, Denmark, Norway and Australia; it will play pretty much everywhere that <a href = "http://www.bbcworldwide.com/">BBC Worldwide</a> licenses TV: if you know three-to-six-year-old children who watch TV, the chances are that you'll see it.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
The series of 26 episodes is based on <a href = "http://www.milkmonitor.com/">Lauren Child</a>'s beautifully written and illustrated books, in which the patient, good-natured Charlie narrates stories about his little sister Lola. It's unusual in its use of children for the characters' voices; it feels fresher and more relaxed than most children's TV. John Greswell from <a href = "http://www.mpmlondon.co.uk/">MPM Music</a> wrote most of the incidental music for the episodes, and helped us enormously with the theme tune arrangement.

To see the titles with our soundtrack, go to the production company's <a href = "http://www.charlieandlola.com/">official site for the series</a>, choose 'clips' and then 'titles'.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Copper Beeches in Delly End
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0

DATE: 06/19/2005 11:18:39 PM
-----
BODY:
We moved here in December 2004, the middle of the English winter. Here's a shot from our bedroom window on a frosty morning just before Christmas - it was so cold that I couldn't keep the window open for more than a few seconds at a time.

-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<img src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/frosty-beeches.jpg" alt="Beech trees in Delly End, December 2004" title="Beech trees in Delly End, December 2004" width="592" height="393" style="padding:4px; border:1px solid #ddd;"/>

Even before Matilda was born I felt that I had a paternal responsibility to learn the names of our native fauna. But I've made little progress, and even if I'd thought about it, I wouldn't have know what to expect when the trees that dominate the green in front of our house came into leaf. It happens so quickly - we came back after a weekend away and the two bare trees of the same height and shape had been replaced by these:

<img src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/copper-beech.jpg" alt="Beech trees in Delly End, June 2004" title="Beech trees in Delly End, June 2004" width="592" height="385" style="padding:4px; border:1px solid #ddd;"/>

They are beech trees, I now know. The one on the left is a common beech, the other is a copper beech. Even after a few weeks, the copper beech has lost a little of its purple lustre; even so, this photograph hasn't captured its intense dark glow. The camera also fails to record the slight difference in hue between the tree on the green and the one to its right, which is just within in the bounds of the manor house (whose topiary and walls you can just see through the glass of our window). I was thinking today that the best way to represent these trees would be with a five second loop of high definition video, to capture the way the colours shift in the breeze.

When you learn about something, you start noticing it everywhere: there was a story on the <a href = "http://www.bbc.co.uk/radio4/today/">Today Programme</a> last week that beeches in England are <a href = "http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/uk_news/england/4089044.stm" title ="BBC coverage">under threat from climate change</a>. It's very affecting, the idea of these beautiful, ancient plants failing to adapt to our cheap flights and big cars.

P.S. The monument in these pictures is a peace memorial, built by the lady of the manor to celebrate the safe return of her two sons from the First World War. 
-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: PostgreSQL and XML updated
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 07/10/2005 10:54:50 PM
-----
BODY:
The XML functions for PostgreSQL (introduced <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/postgresql_and_xml.html" title = "Original post about PostgreSQL XML functions">here</a>) have been updated and, as of version 8, ship with the standard distribution of PostgreSQL. The package now includes support for in-database XSLT transformations and a flexible new <em>xpath_table</em> function which evaluates a set of XPath queries and returns the results as a virtual table.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<h4>Installation</h4>

To build the functions, follow the instructions in contrib/xml2. You'll need recent versions of the libxml2 and libxslt libraries somewhere your compiler can see them. We've compiled and used the functions for PostgreSQL 7.4+ under Linux (Red Hat and Debian), Windows and OS X; here's a <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/pg801_windows_xml.zip">Win32 binary</a> with statically linked libxml2 and libxslt libraries. If you get stuck with the installation, do <a href = "mailto:tomdyson [at] spamcop.net">get in touch</a>.

<h4>XSLT support</h4>

An example:

<pre>SELECT xslt_process(article_xml, '/home/tom/standard.xsl')
    AS rendered_article 
FROM t_articles
WHERE article_id = 55;</pre>

A second:

<pre>SELECT xslt_process(article_xml, template_xslt)
    AS rendered_article
FROM t_articles 
INNER JOIN t_templates 
    ON article_template_id = template_id;</pre>

A third:

<pre>SELECT xslt_process('/home/book.xml', styles_xslt, 'title=Herzog')
    AS rendered_book
FROM t_books 
INNER JOIN t_styles
    ON book_style_id = style_id;</pre>

These demonstrate the function signature:

<em>xslt_process(document, stylesheet [,paramlist]) RETURNS text</em>

Document and stylesheet can be URLs or XML strings, which are identified by a leading left angle bracket. The optional <em>paramlist</em> argument is a list of parameter assignments to be used in the transformation, specified in the form 'a=1,b=2'.

<h4>XPath table</h4>

This makes use of the <a href = "http://www.postgresql.org/docs/7.3/static/xfunc-tablefunctions.html">table functions</a> which were introduced in PostgreSQL 7.3. It's an attempted solder for the impedance mismatch of many-elements-per-document XML and one-unit-per-row SQL. 

Here's an example, modified from John's docs:

<pre>SELECT article_id, author, title 
FROM
xpath_table('article_id', 
    'article_xml',
    'articles', 
    '/article/author|/article/title',
    'date_entered > ''2003-01-01'' ') 
AS t_virtual_table(article_id integer, author text, title text);</pre>

The function signature is

<em>xpath_table(key, document, relation, xpaths, criteria)</em>

where <em>key</em> is the column to be used as the primary key of the generated table; <em>document</em> is the name of the column containing a blob of XML; <em>relation</em> specifies the table which holds the column with the XML blob; <em>xpaths</em> are multiple, pipe-separated XPath expressions; <em>criteria</em> is the contents of the WHERE clause which constrains the generation of the virtual table (use 1=1 to return all rows).
-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:
PostgreSQL, XML, XSLT, XPath, XSL, Postgres 
-----

<img alt="The organ of Magdalen College Chapel, Oxford" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/magdalen-organ.jpg" width="160" height="210" style="padding:4px; border:1px solid #ddd; margin:4px;" align = "right" />The first was on Friday: <a href = "http://www.soundofnorthwood.com">Northwood</a>'s debut, which went as well as we could have hoped.
<br /><br />
The second was on Saturday, at Magdalen College, Oxford, where I played the organ at <a href = "http://www.torchbox.com/people/nick/" title = "Nick Burch at Torchbox" />Nick</a>'s wedding. It's an extraordinary - to me - instrument, situated halfway to the vaulted ceiling of the cool, sombre chapel. The porter gives you the key, and you climb up the stone steps that lead from a small wooden door to the left of the organ screen. I had a scrap of paper with the locations of all the switches: one for the light, two for the bellows, three more for the CCTV cameras which tell you what's happening below. The shelves and floors around the keyboards are littered with the half exotic, half familiar detritus of serious organists: untidy stacks of Bach chorales, a radio controlled clock with a BBC Performances sticker on the front, coffee cups, a nasty plastic hobgoblin holding an old key, a notebook containing pencilled messages about squeaky flute stops, an old copy of the <em>Gormenghast</em> trilogy, a discarded gown.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Colour Management for the web
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: textile_1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 08/07/2005 09:19:39 PM
-----
BODY:
Reproducing photographic colours on the web is harder than it ought to be. This is the workflow I'm using with a <a href = "http://www.dpreview.com/reviews/nikond50/" title = "Nikon D50">new camera</a> and a clean installation of Photoshop: 
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
* Shoot in Adobe RGB. This is a 'high gamut' colour space; it captures more colour information and will withstand more destructive adjustments to levels, hue and saturation. The principle of capturing and using as much source information as possible is true for all digital media - that's why sound engineers record and edit with sample rates of 192 kHz even though they have to downsample the final mix to 44 kHz for domestic CD players. Most digital SLRs will have a colour space setting, which you just need to change once and forget about (note that if you're only capturing 8 bit images, the advantage of using a higher gamut colour space is reduced).
* Edit in Adobe RGB. In Photoshop, this means setting the 'Working Space' for RGB to Adobe RGB and specifiying that embedded colour spaces (the ones coming from your newly configured camera) should be preserved. Make sure that the colour space doesn't get converted during the RAW import, if you're shooting in RAW.
* Convert to <a href = "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SRGB">sRGB</a>. You should do this as late as possible. In Photoshop, choose Image / Mode / Convert to Profile (not Assign Profile).
* Save the final image with an embedded ICC profile. This adds about 3Kb to the JPG, and at <a href = "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/August_2005">the time of writing</a> is only recognised by Safari, OmniWeb and Internet Explorer on the Mac. Embedding the profile is unfortunately necessary because even the <em>absence</em> of colour space information is handled inconsistently by browsers: most default to sRGB; Safari uses your current monitor profile. If you don't care about Mac users and you do care about the extra 3Kb, you can skip this step.

These steps should ensure reasonably faithful colour reproduction across browsers, and since most settings are saved between sessions, the only addition to your workflow is the profile conversion immediately prior to export. Sadly they do not address the issue of gamma variance, which I hardly like to mention... in brief, images are little brighter on most Mac monitors than on most non-Mac monitors (including TVs). The only solution, if you're a Mac user, is to save your images a little brighter than you want, and vice-versa for everyone else. Photoshop has soft-proofing tools which can help with this.  

Finally, here are three photos from the weekend, at home, in the garden and punting on the Cherwell.

<img alt="Matilda eating her supper" title="Matilda eating her supper" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/matilda-eating-0009.jpg" width="592" height="402" class = "greyborder" />

<img alt="Sofia and Kristine in the garden" title="Sofia and Kristin Maria in the garden" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/sofia-kristine-0016.jpg" width="592" height="394" class = "greyborder" />

<img alt="Tom and Alice in a punt by Christchurch meadows" title="Tom and Alice in a punt by Christchurch meadows" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/tom-alice-punt-0090.jpg" width="592" height="437" class = "greyborder" />

-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:
colour management, color management, colour space, color space, Adobe RGB, sRGB, photos, web, gamma

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Peastat
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: textile_1
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 09/11/2005 11:45:26 PM
-----
BODY:
Peastat is a simple, free, 'live' web stats analyser.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
Peastat works differently to other web stats tools: it looks at the last chunk of your log file to create real-time summaries of recent user activity. What you lose in trend analysis - which you're probably already getting from Analog/Webalizer/AWStats/Google Analysis - you gain in focus on what your users are doing right now. 

h4. Peastat Features

* Simple - application, instructions and configuration are included in one file. No database required.
* Free and <a href = "http://www.gnu.org/licenses/gpl.txt" title = "GPL license text">open source</a>
* Atom 1.0 support - monitor recent activity through your newsreader
* Referrer tracking, with search engine query analysis
* Simple path analysis 
* Cached DNS lookups
* No need for JavaScript bugs or PHP includes

h4. System Requirements

* Python 2.1+ available as CGI
* Read access to your log files, in Apache extended/combined format

Linux/BSD/OS X hosts typically support both requirements.

h4. Installation

# Configure the 'logfile' and 'rooturl' values
# Upload pea.py somewhere it can be executed on your web server (e.g. your cgi-bin)
# Make pea.py executable (set its permissions to 755)

h4. Usage

* Point your browser to http://yoursite/cgi-bin/pea.py
* Point your Atom-enabled newsreader to http://yoursite/cgi-bin/pea.py?atom=true

h4. Example

<a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/cgi-bin/pea.py">Peastat for throwingbeans.org</a>

h4. Download

Peastat 0.2 can be downloaded <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/pea.py.txt">here</a>.

h4. Version history

0.2, 18th December, 2005

* Stop rewarding referrer spam
* Simple AJAX library for future use
* Handle user agents whose names include escaped quotes
* Recognise Yahoo searches
* Handle URLs with ampersands correctly
* Time execution of the overview screen
* Don't break on fake referrers
* Improve error handling on tailing log file
* Distinguish links to visited IP details pages with CSS
* Rename from peastat.py to pea.py

0.1, 11th September, 2005

* First public release

h4. FAQ

<ol><li>The name of my log file changes periodically - how do I tell Peastat where to find it?

Format a string for the current date with Python's <a href = "http://docs.python.org/lib/module-time.html">time module</a>, and insert it in the <em>logfile</em> setting: 

<pre>year_slash_month = time.strftime('%Y/%m') # e.g. '2005/12'
logfile = "/var/log/apache/" + year_slash_month + "/access_log"</pre></li>

<li>How do I tell Peastat to ignore referrals from search engines?

Currently the only way to do this is to edit the <em>ignorelines</em> pattern. For example:

<pre>ignorelines = re.compile('(google)|(yahoo)\.co').search</pre></ol>

h4. Acknowledgements

<ul><li>Contributions:

Martin Stricker
Philippe Normand
Juanjo Navarro Mínguez</li>

<li>Suggestions and error reports:

Nick Burch

<img alt="30-seconds-thumb.jpg" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/30-seconds-thumb.jpg" width="160" height="160" class="greyborder" align="right" />Darwin invited Sofia and me to crew for a balloon trip on Saturday morning. 'Crewing' means helping to transport, inflate and launch the balloon, before following it round the country in a car for an hour, meeting it in a field somewhere and packing it all away again.<br /><br />We started in Botley park, south Oxford, at 6 o'clock on a chilly end-of-summer morning. It takes ten minutes to unfurl the envelope (the big fabric part of the balloon) on the ground, taking care not to rip the fragile material; another ten to inflate it with cold air from a powerful fan running off a diesel generator; five more to heat up the air, climb in and take off. Here it is, from start to finish, in <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/albums/2005/september/balloon/">ten photos</a>. <br /><br />In other news, Alice had her first birthday on Friday. AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Carbon Compensation
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: __default__
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: green
CATEGORY: green

DATE: 11/01/2005 10:59:47 PM
-----
BODY:
I've attempted to compensate for the carbon emissions resulting from our recent flights to Greece and Denmark by funding a proportionate amount to sustainable energy and reforestation projects. I used an Oxford-based organisation called <a href = "http://www.climatecare.org/">Climate Care</a>, recommended by Nick, who neutralised the carbon output of his stag weekend to Barcelona, G8-style. 
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
Climate Care have good online <a href = "http://www.climatecare.org/Individuals/index.cfm">CO<sub>2</sub> calculators</a> and an impressively detailed algorithm for determining the emissions from air travel:

<blockquote>"In summary, for long haul we take the average fuel burn figures for a Boeing 747 and an Airbus A360 as published by the EU. We divide this by the average number of seats (not occupied seats) and also subtract the amount of freight carried by the average long haul aircraft. We double the amount of CO2 emitted to take account of the enhanced atmospheric impacts of aviations. We then calculate the great circle distance between the airports in question. A similar method is used for short haul, except that we use a Boeing 737 as the reference aircraft."</blockquote>

It's not clear how this tonnage figure is monetised, or how the carbon sequestering effects of their projects are calculated, but on the whole Climate Care give the impression of an organisation doing the right thing. 
-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:
carbon neutral, carbon neutralisation, carbon neutralization, climate care, carbon emissions
-----

For archivists: this is a <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/audio/lido-charlie-and-lola.mp3">rough early version</a> of the theme tune, one of three that Søren and I presented to Tiger Aspect when we pitched for the job. It was hastily labelled the 'Lido' theme, because we finished the main melody after spending an afternoon at <a href = "http://www.chippylido.co.uk/">Chipping Norton's lido</a> (strapline: "More than just a heated swimming pool").<br /><br />Alice learned to stand up on her own this week. She pushes herself up from a crouch, arms out like a surfer, and looks around happily for congratulations. A few seconds later she falls heavily on her fat little bottom and starts again. Here's a <a href="http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/alice-upright.html" onclick="window.open('http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/alice-upright.html', 'popup', 'width=320,height=240,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0'); return false">nine second clip</a> from my mobile.

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Molokheya
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 11/13/2005 11:35:02 PM
-----
BODY:
<img alt="molokheya" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/molokheya.jpg" width="168" height="132" align="right"/>
This ingredient is the eponymous hero of a staple meal in our household. Molokheya is a green herb, grown for its leaf in the Middle East, and for its stem in India. We have two or three frozen packs delivered every few months by <a href = "http://throwingbeans.org/albums/portraits/samir.html" alt = "Samir Tadros">Sofia's father</a>, who gets them from a friend at his Coptic church, who buys them from an eastern delicatessen in Plymouth. We heat the defrosted herbs in water with lots of garlic and a few granules of a strange-smelling incense; after twenty minutes it takes on a glutinous texture, like okra<!--(this slimeyness comes from <a href = "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mucilage">mucilage</a>, I've just learned)-->. The thick green stew is poured over white rice and boiled chicken; any remainder is served hot with pieces of bread in a bowl the next day. It has a rich, wholesome flavour unlike anything else we eat.<br /><br />Molokheya evokes Sofia's memories of childhood meals in Alexandria, and it's a family favourite in Delly End. As we place the food on the table, Matilda likes to chant its exotic name in hushed, sing-song tones: "mo-lo-<em>hee</em>-ya".
-----

-----

KEYWORDS:
Molokhiya, Molohiya, Mulukhiyah, Molehiya, Molocheiya

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: The Last Cassette
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 11/20/2005 10:48:11 PM
-----
BODY:
I've been listening to a clutch of battered old cassettes which were unearthed during the last domestic reshuffle. They're all TDK SA90s, which were the blank tapes of choice for the cassette compilation connoisseur. The age of compact cassettes is pretty much over now, and gone with it is the rich culture of personal compilations. The biggest disadvantage of tape media compared to CDs, MP3s and vinyl - its lack of support for random access - was also its most attractive quality for the obsessive compiler, for whom the technological advances of skip and shuffle were anathema to his subtle segues, threaded motifs and surprising adjuncts.
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<br /><br />
In my twenties, the receipt of a cassette from Adam or Sofia, Mihai or Jacob - often creatively packaged, always wittily titled - was a significant cultural event, presaging hours of headphone analysis. But making tapes was even better; like DJing in slow motion, with one person on the dancefloor. One of the SA90s I've been playing this week was the last tape I even made; an unfinished eight-year-old masterpiece, intended for Mihai and starting with a track of organic electronica with an interesting varispeed effect that has the strings drifting in and out of tune. I can't remember what this was, and I'll never know because the record it would have been copied from was stolen along with everything else in 2000. Following this, a lovely Zimbabwean mbira song with grunted basso profundo vocals, a Charles Mingus tune, something that sounds like Luke Vibert, Andras Schiff playing the F minor prelude from Bach's first 48, 'Wind Chimes' by the Beach Boys, and <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/audio/this-way.mp3" title = "This way, I can be sure of it">this</a>: ninety seconds of late night introspection from my parents' house circa 1997; two quivering voices dubbed over something like the riff from A Love Supreme, played on their big old German upright piano and recorded on my cassette four track - you can hear the rich tape distortion on the loud bits of the piano solo.
<br /><br />
The track listing sounds self-conciously eclectic (I remember this concern), but there's something consistent in the complilation; a sort of detachment. I'll send it to you, Mihai.
-----

BODY:
I've made a short screencast to demonstrate <a href = "http://www.djangoproject.com/">Django</a>, a Python framework for rapid web development which we've been evaluating at Torchbox. It's not intended as a tutorial - aspects of Django's API are likely to change before its forthcoming 1.0 release, and the project website already provides excellent <a href = "http://www.djangoproject.com/documentation/">documentation</a> - but as an introduction to some of the basic functionality. Areas covered include:
<ul>
<li>Setting up a project</li>
<li>Designing the model</li>
<li>Installing the administration interface</li>
<li>Customising administration screens</li>
<li>URL dispatching</li>
<li>Generic views</li>
<li>Django templates</li>
</ul>
The screencast is encoded with the extraordinary H.264 codec; you'll need QuickTime 7 or <a href = "http://www.videolan.org/vlc/">VLC</a> to watch it. There's a rather breathy soundtrack, but it should make sense without it. If you're having problems viewing the screencast or you're interested in an alternative format, let me know.<br /><br />
<a href = "http://tom.dyson.name/django-qt7-narrated.mov">Django in Seven Minutes</a> (H.264/AAC, 7.4 MB)
<br /><br />
Update: here's a <a href = "http://www.throwingbeans.org/video/django-flash.html">Flash-encoded version</a>, which is lower quality and nearly double the file size (13.5 MB).

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: A Bach Christmas
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 12/24/2005 10:18:16 PM
-----
BODY:
<img src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/jsbach.jpg" alt="Bach" width="160" height="197" align="right" style="padding:4px; border:1px solid #ddd; margin:4px;"/>My Christmas has been marked strongly by Radio 3's <a href = "http://www.bbc.co.uk/radio3/bach/highlights.shtml">Bach marathon</a>, ten days continuous broadcasting of Bach's complete output.
<br /><br />
Highlights for me have included the intensely chromatic cantata <a href = "http://www.jsbach.org/bwv228.html">Fürchte dich nicht</a>, more Ligeti than Leipzig cantor; Emma Kirkby and Christopher Hogwood's Wedding Cantatas; Glen Gould's rockstar 1955 Goldberg Variations (having previously disdained this recording for its strong injection of performer personality and the Keith Jarrett groans, I was infected by its young-man-virtuousity); Joseph Joachim's 1903 recording of selected violin partitas; Roger Norrington's B Minor Mass from the 2000 Proms.
<br /><br />
My introduction to Bach came when I was thirteen, at the hands of <a href = "http://www.gilestv.com/rants2/">Giles Hogben</a>. Giles was a new school friend and a violin prodigy; he played me Bach's sonatas and partitas in the chapel of <a href = "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_King%27s_School%2C_Canterbury">St Augustine's Abbey</a>, and the Brandenburg Concertos on his fancy-pants CD player (fifteen years later he played Bach at my wedding). Around the same time, I sang as a treble in a performance of the St John Passion under the choirmaster <a href = "http://www.bach-cantatas.com/Bio/Rose-Barry.htm">Barry Rose</a>. Since then, I've listened to Bach's music more than to anyone else's: the 48s, the Goldberg Variations, the cello suites, the Art of Fugue, the Passions. I know this sounds pompous, but I believe that his art is the greatest human achievement. <br /><br />Happy Christmas!
-----

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Les Grands Montets
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 02/12/2006 10:42:25 PM
-----
BODY:
<img alt="les-montets-mono.jpg" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/les-montets-mono.jpg" width="592" height="160" alt = "Les Grands Montets" class = "greyborder" />This is <a href = "http://www.flickr.com/photos/ollywillans/">Olly's</a> photograph of the view from Les Grands Montets. It's the knee-weakening start of an 8km descent into the Chamonix valley, 2100m drop in altitude, which was the highlight of my trip. 
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<br /><br />You start by clattering awkwardly down the long run of metal steps from the cable car building to a small platform of snow, where you fix your skis and nervously adjust your goggles. From here there's a steep, narrow passage to the top of the first main run; I was happy to side-slip down this with the rest of our group. Now you can see your route, dropping round the back of the mountain with the wide, bluey Argentières glacier on your right, then cutting over a ridge back onto the main slope, which leads bumpily to the top of La Herse, where you can take a gentler but fast red down to the busy station at Lognan. As your altitude drops, the exhilaration diminishes as gradually as the pleasurable anticipation of a demi pression - taken with your piste-conquering friends on a sunlit terrace, boots comfortably propped up in front of you - grows.
-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:
Les Grands Montets, Argentière, Chamonix Valley

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Beautiful Soup
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 03/07/2006 10:09:40 AM
-----
BODY:
I've been using <a href = "http://www.crummy.com/software/BeautifulSoup/">Beautiful Soup</a>, Leonard Richardson's very forgiving HTML parser, in a couple of recent work projects. This software is so good, you want to indulge the author's <a href = "http://www.crummy.com/2005/12/02/0">peanut brittle plans</a>. 
-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<br /><br />Here's an example of Beautiful Soup in action, fetching the titles of all the posts from this blog. There's a recent <a href = "http://www.crummy.com/software/RubyfulSoup/">Ruby port</a>, but I'm using the Python version:
<br />
<pre>import urllib
from BeautifulSoup import BeautifulSoup
archives_url = 'http://throwingbeans.org/archives.html'
archives_html = urllib.urlopen(archives_url).read()
soup = BeautifulSoup(archives_html)
for h3 in soup.fetch('h3'): 
	print h3.a.string</pre>
The first project spiders two levels of the <a href = "http://www.mssociety.org.uk/">Multiple Sclerosis Society</a>'s site, pulling out related links and rewriting pages for use on a 'Knowledge Store' CD, which helpdesk staff will refer to during support telephone calls. The second sidesteps an interface deficiency in our content management system, and allows me to rapidly republish swathes of content by simulating a robot editor. With screenscraping software this good, who needs APIs?
-----

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: mtraffic.org
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 0
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: tech
CATEGORY: tech

DATE: 03/19/2006 11:42:57 PM
-----
BODY:
<a href = "http://mtraffic.org/">mtraffic.org</a> is a new service providing free UK traffic updates for your mobile phone. It's a simplified, cached and searchable view of the BBC's <a href = "http://www.bbc.co.uk/rd/projects/tpeg/">TPEG feed</a>. mtraffic is designed to be<br />
<ul>
<li>Fast: queries run against a parsed representation of the traffic data; the cache is flushed when a request arrives x seconds after the modification time stamp stored in the persisted feed; the BBC's feed publishes ETags and Last-Modified headers, which are respected by the fetcher; markup is minimal.</li>
<li>Accessible: search results are returned in lightweight, compliant XHTML, which should render reliably on all modern mobile browsers.</li>
<li>Convenient: frequent journeys can be checked with short, stable URLs, e.g. <a href = "http://mtraffic.org/m25">mtraffic.org/m25</a>.</li>
</ul>
mtraffic is written in Python, and is currently running on my <a href = "http://www.bytemark.co.uk/r/naive/">UML machine</a> with Apache 2 and mod_python. If you'd like the sources or you have a bug report, please get in touch.  
-----
EXTENDED BODY:

-----
EXCERPT:

-----
KEYWORDS:
uk traffic updates, mobile traffic news, free uk traffic

AUTHOR: tom
TITLE: Lionel Grigson
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: 0
ALLOW PINGS: 0
PRIMARY CATEGORY: rec
CATEGORY: rec

DATE: 04/02/2006 11:45:00 PM
-----
BODY:
<img alt="lionel-grigson.jpg" src="http://www.throwingbeans.org/images/lionel-grigson.jpg" width="592" height="141" class = "greyborder" alt = "Lionel Grigson's Jazz Chord Book" /><br />This is an excerpt from <em>Lionel Grigson's Jazz Chord Book</em>, my favourite collection of jazz changes. I discovered this book when I was a shy sixteen year old on school holidays in Hastings, East Sussex, where I followed the town's rich but mostly unattended bebop scene. The musicians I watched (nursing a pint of Guinness, hoping I might be asked to sit in, as long as it was on something simple) all played from Lionel's book; one of them, the 'doughty bopper' Pete Burden, is namechecked in the introduction. Liane Carroll, an excellent pianist and singer who filled the small, empty rooms with passionate lyrics and scats, delivered in an uncompromisingly transatlantic accent, was the star of the scene. I see she won two <a href = "http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/jazzawards2005/winners.shtml">BBC Jazz Awards</a> last year, and that excerpts from her last two albums are <a href = "http://www.splashpointrecords.com/LianeCarroll/Music.html">available to download</a>.

-----
EXTENDED BODY:
<br /><br />
Just like these south coast luminaries, I covered my copy of <em>LGJCB</em> in brown paper, and although it didn't get much wear in the first few years, I'm glad I was such an impressionable youth. The third edition is still available from <a href = "http://www.jazzwise.com/catalog/product_info.php?products_id=708">Jazzwise Publicatons</a>, but it's a sad replica of the first two; Lionel's careful, legible handwriting has been replaced with crude typesetting, and many of his precious alternative progressions were dropped to fit the format. If you have a copy of the second edition, maybe you could help me digitise it for future generations.
-----
